### 2. Release notes

* \*\*v2.1:\*\*Helps marketers optimize their automated flows with node-level performance tracking. It unlocks basic needs before entering the future journey phase.
* **v2.2**: to be update

### 3. Goal (v3.0)

Customer Value

* **Handle More Marketing Scenarios**: Easily **implement a wider range of campaigns** and customer communications.
* **Save Time with Automation**: **Reduce manual work** by **automating key marketing communications**.
* **Smarter Marketing with AI**: Future AI helps **work more efficiently** and achieve **better results at a lower cost**.

Business Value

* **Win More Deals**: Attract clients and **capture MA budgets** with multi-channel/AI features, creating **upsell opportunities**.
* **Prevent Churn**: Make MAAC essential with top automation and results, **increasing stickiness** to **prevent churn**.
* **Secure Future with AI**: AI automation offers a unique value for **upselling** and our market leadership.

### 4. Background

* Our current journey feature has not improved for a while, and many users have asked for updates (see [Appendix1- Requirement Analysis](prd-journey-from-2.1-to-3.0+.md#_wz1xf04lqsfs)).
* Most competitors (e.g. Omnichat, Omnisegment, BotBonnie) already offer **multi-channel marketing automation**, and this is now a basic industry standard. If we don‚Äôt catch up, we risk losing users and increasing churn (If fact, we already had some churn cases because of MA).

### 5. Strategy

MAAC‚Äôs position is a Omnichannel Marketing Automation platform powered by AI.

**Why it's important**

The marketing automation market is fiercely competitive. Users demand robust automation for efficient, personalized multi-channel engagement. Without advanced journey capabilities, MAAC cannot meet these essential user needs or scale effectively, risking falling behind competitors.

**Why now**

Our current marketing automation limitations have contributed to customer churn. However, AI technology has matured significantly, offering a pivotal opportunity. This is the moment to invest in a next-generation, AI-powered Customer Journey solution, not just to address current gaps but to innovate and leapfrog the competition.

**How to winÔºöBetter-Different-New**

After conducting a competitor analysis (see [Appendix3- Competitor analysis](prd-journey-from-2.1-to-3.0+.md#_aldywm9g3jj5)), our strategy focuses on four key pillars to establish MAAC as a leading Journey solution:

* **Catchup: Quickly Add More Channels to Meet Basic Market Needs.**
  * MAAC will first deliver **Quick Wins** for immediate user value, such as better performance insight and improved triggers (see [Appendix 1- Requirement Analysis](prd-journey-from-2.1-to-3.0+.md#_wz1xf04lqsfs)). It will then **Expand to Multi-Channel** by building foundational IA and infrastructure, launching a second channel quickly, and potentially **outsourcing** further channel additions (3rd, 4th, 5th, and more) to rapidly match competitor offerings and reduce churn.
* **Better: Use MAAC's LINE Strength for Superior Multi-Channel Journeys.**
  * MAAC will make LINE the core of its multi-channel strategy. Other channels will support LINE by either bringing users _to_ LINE or by addressing communication gaps where LINE may not be the most effective tool. For example, SMS can be used to attract new users who are then transitioned to LINE for loyalty programs, or email can be used to reactivate inactive LINE users.
* **Different: Offer Unique Journeys with MAAC + CAAC 2-Way Conversations.**
  * MAAC will differentiate itself by moving beyond the one-way messages common in most MA tools. By combining its marketing automation platform (MAAC) with CAAC (its 2-way conversational AI platform), MAAC can utilize rich chat data to create truly interactive journeys. For instance, special marketing care can be triggered after a customer service chat, or products can be suggested based on needs users expressed during conversations.
* **New: Build a 10x Better Experience with AI-First Principles**
  * With an **AI-first strategy**, MAAC will identify where AI can **drastically improve upon traditional Marketing Automation's shortcomings**. If both AI and traditional solutions can solve a problem, **AI solutions will be prioritized when they offer substantial benefits**. For instance, an "AI Copilot" will enable faster, more customized journey creation than standard templates, boosting effectiveness. The user-friendliness of these AI tools will be carefully validated (see [Appendix 4- AI features](prd-journey-from-2.1-to-3.0+.md#_ezc7932tihc0)).

### 7. TA - Problem - Solution - Selling Points

**Key Differentiators once MAAC Journey evolved to v3.0**

Aligned with MAAC‚Äôs journey strategy, here are the key differentiators by Better-Different-New framework

* **Better: LINE expertise** MAAC's competitive advantage lies in its unparalleled LINE expertise, which remains its foundational strength. Even as MAAC expands to multi-channel capabilities, these new avenues will be designed to enhance and maintain a strong connection to the core LINE experience, offering a more cohesive and effective journey than competitors who lack this deep specialization.
* **Different: MAAC (1-way) + CAAC (2-way)** MAAC distinguishes itself from typical marketing automation platforms through its CAAC . This focus on genuine 2-way conversations transforms automated journeys into dynamic, interactive dialogues‚Äîa unique strength MAAC will fully leverage to create more engaging and responsive customer interactions.
* **New: AI-first** Unlike traditional multi-channel journeys, MAAC's key innovation is the deep integration of AI. This makes artificial intelligence the standout feature of its journey evolution, driving smarter automation and more personalized customer experiences.

**TA- Problem- Solution - Selling points by version**

TAÔºöMarketers, CRM Specialists

| **Problems**                                                                             | **Solutions**                                                    | **Selling Points**                                                                                  |
| ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| **Complex & Slow Journey Setup**: Hard to create journeys; no easy start with templates. | 3.0: AI Journey generation for faster, simpler setup.            | Easier and faster to setup by using MAAC AI co-pilot                                                |
| **Single Channel Limitation**: LINE-only; cannot engage on other channels.               | 2.5+: Multi-channel integration (SMS, WhatsApp, Web chat, etc.). | LINE-centric multi-channel: Seamlessly extend LINE strategies, enhancing with CAAC across channels. |
| **Inflexible Triggers**: Hard to set specific/recurring times or complex behaviors.      | 2.2: time-based triggers and rules (Countdown)                   | Precise, flexible LINE scheduling.                                                                  |
| **Limited Journey Actions**: Few action types beyond sending messages.                   | 2.5+: More actions (Tags, CAPI, API, CDH integration).           | Enable users to achieve more marketing scenarios.                                                   |
| **Lack of Performance Insight**: Low visibility on journey step performance.             | 2.1: Node metrics (traffic, sent, opens) & node-based segments.  | Table stakes: enable users to view the detailed node performance.                                   |
| **Inefficient Journey Updates**: Manual changes are slow and error-prone.                | 3.5: AI-assisted updates & better UI for easier changes.         | Simplified journey management: AI suggests efficient changes and improvement.                       |
| **Limited Optimization Tools**: No A/B testing or dynamic adjustment tools.              | 3.5: AI Journey Optimizer & A/B testing.                         | AI optimization tailored: Uses MAAC's data & CAAC context, surpassing standard A/B tests.           |

### 9.1 Scope (v2.1)

* Node performance
* Technical improvement (throughput)

#### Success metric

* Increase in the number of active journeys by X% within 3 months post-launch.
  * current journey adoption rate:
* Y% of marketers report satisfaction with the new analytics and trigger capabilities (via survey).

#### Feature list

* [A - View Node Performance \[P0\]](prd-journey-from-2.1-to-3.0+.md#_uhhotlic3z3p)

#### A - View Node Performance Data \[P0]

#### User story

* As a marketer, I want to see detailed performance metrics (including traffic count, message sent, and open count) for each journey node, so that I can understand how each step is performing and identify areas for improvement.

#### Flow

1. The user enters the "Journey" section in MAAC.
2. **Empty state**: Before users publish the journey, there are no node performance metrics in the journey editor page and journey view page.
3. **Display metrics**: Once users create a journey, after a while (wait for data update), each node will display key metrics in both journey editor and view pages, and the performance metrics summary will display in the top area of the journey view page.
4. **Edit node details:** When users click ‚Äúpause and edit‚Äù, user can edit the node details (note: users are not able to create a new node or delete a node after publishing the journey) and there are two types of cases need to handle
5. Case 1: duplicate. When users change the trigger type (e.g.: from tag trigger to open LINE msg), users will see the pop-up dialog with ‚Äúduplicate‚Äù and ‚Äúcancel‚Äù options. 1. If users click the ‚Äúduplicate‚Äù button, the system will create a new journey for users. 2. If users click the ‚Äúcancel‚Äù button, the system will go back to the previous step without saving changes.
6. Case 2: kind reminder. When users change the other settings (other than changing the trigger type), users will see the side drawer with ‚Äúsave‚Äù and ‚Äúcancel‚Äù options, and the info to remind users to note the time of this change for before/ after analysis. 1. If users click the ‚Äúsave‚Äù button, the system will save the changes. 2. If users click the ‚Äúcancel‚Äù button, the system will go back to the previous step without saving changes.

#### Spec![](<../../../.gitbook/assets/Unknown image (60)>)

* **1.Performance summary (in view page)**
  * **Categorize by theme**
    * Open rate
      * Message pushed
      * Open rate
        * Open count
    * CTR
      * CTR
        * Click counts
      * Unique CTR
        * Unique clicks
    * Revenue (GA4 plan is required)
      * Add to cart
      * Orders
      * Revenue
* **2.Node performance metric for different node types**

| Node Type | Trigger Node                                                                                                                                               | Rule Node                                                                                                                          | Action Node (Send LINE message)                                                                                                                                             |
| --------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Metrics   | - # of trigger events - Traffic Counts - Unique contacts                                                                                                   | - # of rule events - Traffic counts - Unique contacts                                                                              | Engagement events - Traffic Counts - Unique contacts - Message pushed - Open counts - Click counts - Unique clicks Conversion events - Orders (from GA) - Revenue (from GA) |
| Note      | Trigger type: - add tag - open msg - page view (GA) - add to cart (GA) - purhcase (GA) If users do not purchase GA module, then they won‚Äôt have GA events. | Rule type: Rule - Time delay - Scheduled time - Yes/No Split GA events as rule - page view (GA) - add to cart (GA) - purhcase (GA) | If users do not purchase GA module, then they won‚Äôt have GA events.                                                                                                         |

* Note: in the future, we might have a Web SDK event node. The behavior is similar to the GA Event node.
* **3.Node performance metric for Split**
  * Display the % of traffic counts for each Split
* 4.Metrics should update regularly (update frequency = 1 hour).

#### TC-2: Metric Accuracy

| **ID**      | **Test Description**                                | **Preconditions**                                                                                    | **Steps**                                                                | **Expected Result**                                                                                                               |
| ----------- | --------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------ | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| **TC-2.01** | Validate "Trigger" node metrics.                    | A journey is triggered x times by y unique users.                                                    | 1. Open the journey. 2. View the Trigger node.                           | The node displays "# of trigger events: x" and "Traffic Count: y" (or reflects the precise definition from the data source).      |
| **TC-2.02** | Validate "Action (Send LINE message)" node metrics. | A message node sends to x users. y open it, and z click a link. This generates m orders totaling $n. | 1. Open the journey. 2. View the Action node.                            | The node correctly displays: "Traffic Count: x", "Message Sent: x", "Open count: y", "Click count: z", "Order: m", "Revenue: $n". |
| **TC-2.03** | Validate "Rule" node metrics.                       | x users reach a rule node. y meet the criteria, and z do not.                                        | 1. Open the journey. 2. View the Rule node.                              | The node correctly displays "# of rule events" and "Traffic count: x". The subsequent Splites should show a y% / z% split.        |
| **TC-2.04** | Validate data update frequency.                     | An active journey is running.                                                                        | 1. Trigger a new user to enter the journey. 2. Observe the Trigger node. | The metrics on the node should update to reflect the new data within the specified regular interval (n minutes).                  |

Open the journey.                                      | All performance metric values should be 0.                                                                     |

View the nodes on the empty path. | The Split split should show 0% for that path. All subsequent nodes on that path should show 0 for all metrics. |

### 9.2 Scope (v2.2)

#### Background

**Time-based trigger (target segment) + Add/Remove Tag => unblock segment RM**

* In alignment with the [2025H2- MAAC Product Strategy Narratives](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1TUmfDzsxwUK_NYbteNmKizvC5n-Qt-2QVjzGrRLq2yE/edit?tab=t.0), our goal is to be channel-agnostic rather than channel-specific. Therefore, direct optimization within LINE RichMenu is not a viable path. Instead, we aim to leverage **Journey** to enhance long-term product extensibility and flexibility across channels.
* For the **Segment-based Richmenu** feature, we will **not** make any changes to the existing Richmenu mechanism. Additionally, **reporting** will continue to link back to the original Richmenu functionality for data viewing.

**Requirements**

* Marketers want to tailor the particular segment based on attributes such as CAAC tags, purchase behavior, or multi-tag filters.
* MRR Impact Overview
  * **Confirmed Existing MRR Impact**: JPY: ¬•57,000 with Takeya
  * **Additional Upside**: Potentially significant via OWNDAYS

| **Client**                                                                                                                              | **Type** | **Scenario**                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         | **Feature**                                                                                                                                                                                                                    | **MRR**                                              |
| --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | ---------------------------------------------------- |
| \[JP] [OWNDAYS](https://chatbotgang.slack.com/archives/C05GYFFD5PU/p1740035804169439?thread_ts=1737110722.065419\&cid=C05GYFFD5PU)      | Prospect | **As a brand like OWNDAYS**, I want to **import segments from TreasureData** and use them to **switch Rich Menus** dynamically, so that each segment sees tailored recommendation messages relevant to their profile.**As a brand like Catalog House**, I want to **switch Rich Menus based on purchased products and purchase timing**, so that I can surface relevant post-purchase actions or cross-sell content at the right time. While RM switching via Tag is supported in MAAC, these brands require segment-based RM switching from external data sources‚Äîmaking Segment Trigger the more scalable and automated approach.                                                                                                  | Ability to use created segments via treasuredata directly to switch the display of rich menus.                                                                                                                                 | (TBD - potentially high as it‚Äôs a multi-region deal) |

####

#### Success metric

* Adoption: ‚â• 20% of Orgs whose newly created journeys used any of the new trigger types (e.g., time-based) or new actions (e.g., add/remove tag) at least once within the first 3 months.

#### User Flow

| ![](<../../../.gitbook/assets/Unknown image (61)>) | **Create Segment in MAAC**- Go to **Audience > Segment**- Define the segment conditions (e.g., profile attributes, tags, behavior)**Configure RichMenu Rules**- Go to **Channel > LINE > RichMenu**- Set visibility conditions using tags (e.g., ‚ÄúShow RM A when user has tag X‚Äù)**Set Up Journey with Time-based Trigger**- Go to **Journey**- Choose a **Time-based trigger** (e.g., daily at 9 AM) - Filter to **target a specific segment\*\*\*\*Add Tag Action in Journey**- Add an **"Add Tag"** node - The tag should match the visibility rule set in the RichMenu (e.g., tag X) - This action will dynamically control RichMenu switching**Preview & Activate Journey**- Double-check your journey logic and audience filters - Activate the Journey to start automation |

#### Feature list

* [A - Trigger Node: Time-based Trigger (target specific segment)](prd-journey-from-2.1-to-3.0+.md#_7cwluxddchei)
* [B - Rules Node: Add/Remove Tag](prd-journey-from-2.1-to-3.0+.md#_rq2pcz9o8ese) (Leverage existing Richmenu mechanism)
* [C - Split Node: Open/Click Message](prd-journey-from-2.1-to-3.0+.md#_k1lh8rltnpke)
* [D - Node Performance](prd-journey-from-2.1-to-3.0+.md#_towmpi5i8zal)
* [E - Join LINE event trigger](prd-journey-from-2.1-to-3.0+.md#_34768clluaxi)
* [F - Block LINE event trigger](prd-journey-from-2.1-to-3.0+.md#_6i3g71qwi4ic)

**A - Trigger Node: Time-based Trigger (target specific segment)**

**User story**

* As a marketer, I want to create a journey that triggers based on a specific date and time (e.g., to launch a holiday promotion precisely at midnight), and I also want to set this trigger to recur (e.g., every Monday morning for a weekly update, on the 1st of every month for a newsletter, or every day at a specific time for daily tasks) while targeting a specific segment, so that I can schedule campaigns accurately in advance and automate regular communications without manual setup each time.

**Trigger Node Concept**

* **Journey Event Trigger needs to include time, people, and event. (Who, When, What)**
  * **Time**: At the moment of the event, on a set schedule (e.g., daily/weekly/monthly)
  * **People**: The user who triggered the event, or a defined segment based on CDH attributes.
  * **Event**: Triggered by the user‚Äôs action or automatically by the system.

**Flow**

1. User creates a new journey or edits an existing one.
2. User adds or selects a Trigger node on the canvas.
3. User sets a Time for when the trigger should fire.
4. _(Optional)_ User enables the Repeat checkbox to set up recurrence.
5. _(If Repeat is enabled)_ User configures recurrence options:

* Selects one or more Frequencies:
  * Daily
  * Weekly ‚Üí selects one or more days of the week (e.g., Monday, Wednesday)
  * Monthly ‚Üí selects one or more days of the month (e.g., 1st, 15th)

6. _(Optional)_ User sets an End Recurrence Date or keeps the default ‚ÄúNever‚Äù.
7. User saves the configuration.
8. On the configured Time, the trigger fires and users in the entry segment enter the journey.
9. If recurrence is enabled, the trigger continues to fire at the defined intervals.
10. Users added to the entry segment later will enter on the next valid trigger time.

**Spec**

**| Basic Configuration (Always Shown)**

* **Start Date**
  * _Type_: Date picker (yyyy/MM/dd)
  * _Description_: The date the trigger becomes active or the first occurrence if recurring.
* **Time**
  * _Type_: Time picker (hh:mm)
  * _Description_: The time of day the trigger will fire.
* **Segment**
  * _Type_: Multi-select group (similar as the segment selector in Broadcast)
  * _Description_: The selected contacts the trigger will target.

**| Recurrence Configuration (Shown only if "Repeat" is enabled)**

* **Repeat**
  * _Type_: Checkbox
  * _Description_: Enables recurring trigger behavior.
* **Frequencies**
  * _Type_: Multi-select group (support selecting more than one frequency)
  * _Options_:
    * \*\*Daily:\*\*Fires at the same time every day.
    * \*\*Weekly:\*\*Additional field: **Days of Week** ‚Üí Multi-select dropdown (e.g., Monday, Thursday)
    * \*\*Monthly:\*\*Additional field: **Days of Month**‚Üí Multi-select dropdown or numeric input (e.g., 1, 15, 31)
* **End Recurrence (Optional)**
  * _Options_:
    * **Never** _(default)_
    * **On Date**:
      * _Type_: Date picker
      * _Description_: Last possible day the trigger can fire.

**| Execution Logic**

* On the **Start Date**, the trigger fires at the configured **Time** for all users in the journey's selected entry **segment**.
* If **Repeat** is enabled:
  * The trigger fires repeatedly according to the selected **Frequencies**.
  * Multiple frequency rules may be active in parallel. The trigger should fire **multiple times**, once for each rule that is met. This could cause a user to enter the journey multiple times on the same day.
    * Example: "Every 1st and 15th of the month at 09:00 AM" **AND** "Every Monday at 09:00 AM".
  * If a selected Monthly day (e.g., 31st) does not exist in a given month, the trigger will **not** fire for that month.

**Discussion w/ eng:**[**https://app.asana.com/1/1184020052539844/project/1206764649948244/task/1210692417161648?focus=true**](https://app.asana.com/1/1184020052539844/project/1206764649948244/task/1210692417161648?focus=true)\*\*\*\*We need to evaluate whether updating the segment can be processed within 1 hour. ‚Üí solution ticketnote (ÁõÆÂâçÂáåÊô®ÁöÑ loading ‰πüÂæàÈáçÔºåe.g. ÊØèÂ∞èÊôÇÊ™¢Êü•‰∏ãÂÄã 24 hours ÊòØÂê¶ÊúâÂäüËÉΩÊúÉÁî®Âà∞ÔºâExpectation: 1hour (4M ÂéªÊäìÁ≥ªÁµ±ËÉΩ‰∏çËÉΩÂêÉÔºâ



**B - Action Node: Add/Remove Tag**

**User story**

* As a marketer, I want to automatically add a specific tag to contacts based on their interaction or status at a specific journey node (e.g., tag users as 'Engaged\_PromoX' if they opened the promo message at that node), so that I can easily categorize and identify these contacts for ongoing personalization or future campaigns without necessarily creating a full, separate segment.
* As a marketer, I want to automatically remove a specific tag from contacts based on their interaction or status at a specific journey node (e.g., remove the ‚Äòhigh potential purchase‚Äô tag if they already have completed purchase), so that I can easily manage the effective tags on contacts for better personalization.

**Flow**

1. User selects a specific node on the journey canvas.
2. An option like "Apply Action from Node" is available. User selects "Add/Remove Tag".
3. A modal or interface appears.
4. User defines the **Criteria** for applying the tag (same options as segment creation: "Reached this node," "Opened message," etc.).
5. User selects tag source of MAAC or CAAC
6. User selects an **Existing Tag** from a searchable dropdown list.
7. User confirms the action. The selected tag is applied to all users who currently meet the defined criteria at that node.

**Spec**

* **User Inclusion Criteria:**
  * Once the contacts who reached Node X, then auto add or remove tag.
* **Tag Selection:**
  * Searchable dropdown list to find the desired tag, including MAAC/CAAC/CDH tag source.
  * Support multiple tags, a maximum is 5 tags.
* **Application:**
  * It will automatically tag new users passing through the node after this action is performed.



**C - Split Node: Open/Click Message ‚Üí Removed feature C from v2.2 (combine into interaction node)User Story As a marketer, I want to create a Split in the journey that splits contacts based on whether they have opened or clicked a LINE message sent at the previous step, so that I can deliver more personalized follow-up actions based on their engagement behavior.**

**Flow**

* This Split can only be used immediately after a "Send LINE Message" action node.
* When a user reaches this Split, the system checks if the contact has opened or clicked the LINE message sent at the preceding node.
* Contacts who opened or clicked the message proceed along the "Engaged" path, while those who did not proceed along the "Not Engaged" path.
* Marketers can configure different actions or subsequent nodes for each path accordingly.

**Spec**

* Applicable only to journeys where the previous node is a "Send LINE Message" action.
* Engagement criteria include:
  * Contacts who opened / did not open the message after A Days / B Hours / C Minutes the contact receive the message.
  * Contacts who clicked / did not click the message after A Days / B Hours / C Minutes the contact open the message.
* The Split supports single or multiple LINE message engagements but must be linked directly after the send action node.



**D - Node Performance**

**User Story**

As a marketer, I want to evaluate how scheduled triggers and tag-based actions perform in my journey, so I can:

* Validate whether recurring triggers are effectively reaching my target segment on schedule.
* Confirm whether tag applications/removals are occurring as expected, to maintain accurate contact classification.
* Analyze node-level engagement to iterate on timing and segmentation strategies.

**Flow**

1. Marketer creates or edits a journey with:

* A Time-based Trigger node configured with schedule and recurrence rules.
* One or more Add/Remove Tag Action nodes applied at key journey steps based on behavioral criteria.

2. At each scheduled time, the trigger fires and eligible users enter the journey.
3. As users move through the journey, system applies or removes tags based on defined criteria at the action nodes.
4. Platform logs the node-level performance of both trigger executions and tag applications.
5. Marketer views node performance to analyze:

* Recurring trigger effectiveness (e.g., per date, per recurrence type).
* Execution rate and volume of tag actions (added/removed).
* Overall flow traffic and engagement at each stage.

**Spec**

Scope:

* Trigger Node: Time-based Trigger
* Rules Node: Add/Remove Tag
* Split Node: Open/Click Message

| Metric          | Description                                                            |
| --------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Traffic counts  | Total number of times the trigger has fired (each recurrence counted). |
| Unique contacts | Total unique contacts entering the journey via this trigger.           |

**E - Join LINE event trigger**

**User Story**

As a marketer, I want to trigger a journey the moment a user joins our LINE official account, so that I can immediately engage new followers with a welcome message and show the new friend richmenu, with an introductory offer, or a guided onboarding experience to improve conversion and retention from the very beginning.

**Flow**

1. A user adds the brand's LINE Official Account as a friend.
2. MAAC receives a "follow event" from LINE.
3. This event acts as a trigger for a specific journey.
4. The user who initiated the follow event is immediately entered into the journey to receive the pre-defined sequence of messages or actions.

**Spec**

* **Trigger Condition**: The journey is triggered by the "LINE Event - Add Friend" (Áï∂ËÅØÁµ°‰∫∫Âä†ÂÖ•Â•ΩÂèã).

**F - Block LINE event trigger**

**User Story**

As a marketer, I want to trigger a journey the moment a user blocks our LINE official account, so that I can automatically reach out via alternative channels like email or SMS. This allows me to understand the reason for their departure through a survey, attempt to win them back with a targeted offer, or simply maintain the customer relationship on a different platform, ultimately helping to reduce churn and gather crucial feedback.

**Flow**

1. A user blocks the brand's LINE Official Account.
2. MAAC receives an "unfollow event" from LINE.
3. This event acts as a trigger for a specific journey.
4. The user who initiated the block event is entered into the journey to trigger follow-up actions on other channels (e.g., send an email or SMS).

**Spec**

* Trigger Condition: The journey is triggered by the "LINE Event - Block Friend" (Áï∂ËÅØÁµ°‰∫∫Â∞ÅÈéñÂ•ΩÂèã).

### 9.3 Scope (v2.3) (not for review yet; Lydia WIP)

#### Background

**SDK event trigger/Split + send Retargeting msg => (1) Retargeting P3 - port to journey (2) Real-time Journey be supported by SDK**

This is related to Phase 3 of the [PRD - Retargeting 2.0](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1WOFbt7af3vZiFCPMf41cRHZ7QLzrBiWIeRXOh7Anys4/edit?tab=t.0#bookmark=id.ftxogrdpax4a).We also aim to address the GA4 latency issue within the journey. Additionally, some enterprise clients may have concerns about granting GA4 access permissions. With an SDK integration, they would have more control over what data is shared with CL.

#### Success metric

* Adoption of new trigger or Split types (e.g.: SDK events) and new actions (e.g.: send retargeting msg) in X% of newly created journeys.

#### Feature list

* [SDK event trigger/Split](prd-journey-from-2.1-to-3.0+.md#_54h2iwq9s779)
* [Send retargeting msg](prd-journey-from-2.1-to-3.0+.md#_emmudynq13ku)
* [Node and Report Performance](prd-journey-from-2.1-to-3.0+.md#_ttgi0n6i1fds)

**A - SDK event trigger/Split**

**User story**

* As a marketer, I want to set SDK event triggers or create journey Splites based on real-time customer behavior (e.g., page view, add to cart, purchase), so that I can personalize the journey experience based on whether or not a customer has completed key actions.

**Flow**

_Trigger Node_

1. User opens the Journey Builder interface.
2. In the trigger configuration panel, user selects **‚ÄúSDK Event‚Äù** as the trigger type.
3. A dropdown appears with event options; user chooses one of the following: page\_view, add\_to\_cart, purchase
4. User confirms the selection.
5. The selected SDK event is now set as the entry trigger node of the journey.
6. The journey will start for any user who performs the selected SDK event in real-time.

_Filter / Split Node_

1. User opens the Journey Builder interface.
2. In the filter or Split configuration panel, user selects **‚ÄúSDK Event‚Äù** as the filter or Split type.
3. A dropdown appears with event options; user chooses one of the following: page\_view, add\_to\_cart, purchase
4. User confirms the selection.
5. The selected SDK event is now set as the filter criteria or the Split node of the journey.
6. The journey will auto triage for any user who performs the selected SDK event in real-time.

**Spec**

* **Data source (selectable):**
  * The data source could be a GA4 event or an SDK event.
    * If the clients have both GA4 event and SDK event, then default choose SDK event and support the client to adjust in each journey.
    * If the clients only have GA4, then by default choose the GA4 and show SDK as a greyout option.
    * If the clients only have SDK, then by default choose the SDK and show GA4 as a greyout option.
* **Event type (selectable):**
  * The event type for trigger, filter or Split node could be selected in the dropdown list: page\_view, add\_to\_cart, purchase
* **Future Considerations (not in scope):**
* Allow event properties (e.g., product category, price) as additional conditions.
* Support custom events beyond the 3 default ones.

**B - Send Retargeting msg**

**User Story** As a marketer, I want to send a retargeting message to users who haven‚Äôt completed a purchase action with items in their shopping cart, so that I can bring them back into the purchase funnel and improve conversion rates.

**Flow**

_Send Retargeting Message Node_

* User opens the Journey Builder interface.
* In the action configuration panel, user selects ‚ÄúSend Retargeting Message‚Äù as the action type.
* User configures the message content (e.g., unpaid items).
* User confirms the configuration.
* The action node is now set to send the retargeting message when a user reaches this step in the journey.
* When the journey reaches this node, the system will automatically send the configured message to the user.

**Spec**_Message Content:_

* Configurable using the MAAC message editor.

_Delivery Conditions (optional):_

* Delay sending (e.g., ‚ÄúSend 2 hours after abandonment‚Äù).
* Send only during specific time windows (e.g., 9AM‚Äì9PM user time).

**C - Node and Report Performance**

**User Story**

As a marketer, I want to evaluate how SDK event trigger/Split and Send Retargeting msg perform in my journey, so I can:

* Confirm whether the new nodes are occurring as expected, to maintain accurate contact classification.
* Analyze node-level engagement to iterate on strategies.

**Flow**

1. Marketer creates or edits a journey with SDK event trigger/Split and Send Retargeting msg.
2. At each trigger event happens, the trigger fires and eligible users enter the journey.
3. As users reach the send retargeting msg action node in the journey, system auto send the retargeting message based on defined criteria at the action nodes.
4. Platform logs the node-level performance of both trigger, split and action executions.
5. Marketer views node performance to analyze:

* Trigger effectiveness.
* Execution rate and volume of actions.
* Overall flow traffic and engagement at each stage.

**Spec**

_Scope:_

* Trigger Node: SDK event trigger

| Metric          | Description                                                  |
| --------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------ |
| Traffic counts  | Total number of times the trigger has fired                  |
| Unique contacts | Total unique contacts entering the journey via this trigger. |

* Rules Node: SDK event split

| Metric          | Description                                     |
| --------------- | ----------------------------------------------- |
| Traffic counts  | Total number of times the split has been passed |
| Unique contacts | Total unique contacts pass through this split.  |

* Action Node: Send retargeting message

| Metric          | Description                                         |
| --------------- | --------------------------------------------------- |
| Traffic counts  | Total number of times the action has been reached   |
| Unique contacts | Total unique contacts reach the action              |
| Message sent    | How many messages were sent via this action?        |
| Open count      | How many of the sent messages were opened?          |
| Click ocunt     | How many of the sent messages were clicked?         |
| Order           | How many of orders completed via the sent messages? |
| Revenue         | How much revenue generated via the sent messages?   |

### 9.X Scope (v2.X) (not for review yet; Lydia WIP)

#### Background

**interaction split node + Journey event pipeline for omnichannel**

In the second half of 2025, we aim to transition toward full omnichannel marketing automation. As part of this shift, the interaction split node will serve as one of the foundational building blocks.

In this release, we will enhance the journey event pipeline to support omnichannel scenarios and introduce a new interaction split node. This node allows marketers to assess whether a customer interacted with the previous message (e.g., opened or clicked), enabling them to create split branches based on those behaviors and define follow-up actions tailored to different user segments.

#### Success metric

* Adoption of new interaction split node in X% of newly created journeys.

#### Feature list

* [interaction split node](prd-journey-from-2.1-to-3.0+.md#_a1qkl71v3kt8)
* [Node and Report Performance](prd-journey-from-2.1-to-3.0+.md#_w36cez228ym8)

**A - interaction split node**

**User story**

As a marketer, I want to split the journey based on whether a user opened or clicked the previous message (according to different channels), so that I can deliver personalized follow-up actions depending on their level of engagement.

**Flow**

_interaction split node_

1. Marketer sets up a journey with a message-sending node (e.g., LINE, SMS, Email).
2. Adds an interaction split node immediately after the send message node.
3. In the interaction split node, selects the interaction criteria (e.g., "Message Opened", "Link Clicked").
4. System evaluates user behavior for that specific message.
5. Based on whether the user met the selected criteria, the journey splits into two branches (Yes / No).
6. Each branch can lead to a different follow-up action (e.g., resend, tag, offer incentive).

**Spec**

_Supported Channels_

* LINE, SMS
* Additional channels to be supported in future iterations.

_Supported Events (per channel)_

* LINE: Open, Click
* SMS: Click

_Node Input_

* Must follow immediately after a supported Action Node
* Configurable condition: Open, Click

_Node Output_

* Two split:
  * Yes ‚Äì Users who matched the interaction criteria
  * No ‚Äì Users who did not match the criteria within the defined window

_Time Window for Evaluation_

* Default: 24 hours
* Customizable: 1 to 72 hours

_Limitations_

* Only evaluates interaction with the immediately preceding message node
* Cannot evaluate multiple messages or aggregate interactions across nodes (MVP scope)

**B - Node and Report Performance**

**User Story**

As a marketer, I want to evaluate how the interaction split node performs in my journey, so I can:

* Confirm whether the new nodes are occurring as expected, to maintain accurate contact flow.
* Analyze node-level engagement to iterate on strategies.

**Flow**

1. Marketer creates or edits a journey with the interaction split node.
2. As users reach the interaction split node in the journey, system auto split the contacts based on defined criteria at the split nodes.
3. Platform logs the node-level performance of both split executions.
4. Marketer views node performance to analyze the split traffic and contacts.

**Spec**

_Scope:_

* Interaction split node

| Metric          | Description                                     |
| --------------- | ----------------------------------------------- |
| Traffic counts  | Total number of times the split has been passed |
| Unique contacts | Total unique contacts pass through this split.  |

### 9.X Scope (v2.X) (not for review yet; Lydia WIP)

Time counter trigger + CDH data filter

#### Time counter

#### User story

* As a marketer, I want to create a journey reminder that triggers a set duration before or after a specific reference date (e.g., 1 day prior to an event, 3 days after a purchase for a review request), so that I can automate timely follow-ups.

#### Flow

1. User creates a new journey or edits an existing one.
2. User selects a date-type Custom Field from MAAC (e.g., "Birthday," "Subscription End Date," "Last Purchase Date").
3. User defines the time reminder offset: e.g., 7 days BEFORE "Birthday," or 1 month AFTER "Subscription End Date".
4. User sets the time of day for the trigger.

#### Spec

* Reference Date Field (dropdown of available date-type custom fields).
* Offset Number (integer).
* Offset Unit (Days, Weeks, Months).
* Offset Direction (Before, After).
* Time of day for execution.

Example: To send a birthday greeting: Reference Field = "Birthday", Offset = 0 days (or 1 day Before for pre-greeting), Time = 9:00 AM.

####

#### Node-based Segment or Tag \[P2]

#### User story

* **B.1 Segment creation \[P1]**
  * As a marketer, I want to be able to create a new MAAC segment of users based on their interaction or status at a specific journey node (e.g., users who reached node X, users who opened the message at node Y), so that I can conduct targeted follow-up actions or analysis.

**B.1. Segment creation \[P1]**

#### Flow

1. User views an active or completed journey with performance metrics.
2. User selects a specific node on the journey canvas or from a performance view.
3. An option like "Apply Action from Node" (or a direct "Create Segment") is available. User selects "Create Segment".
4. A modal or interface appears.
5. User defines the **Criteria** for including users in the segment (e.g., "Reached this node," "Opened message sent from this node," "Did NOT open message from this node").
6. User names the new segment.
7. User saves the segment. The segment (containing users who met the criteria at the time of creation) becomes available in the MAAC Segments list for other uses.

#### Spec

* **User Inclusion Criteria (selectable):**
  * Users who reached Node X.
  * Users who were sent a message from Node Y.
  * Users who opened a message from Node Z.
  * Users who did _not_ open a message from Node Z (but were sent it).
* The created segment is a static snapshot of users who met the criteria at the time of segment creation.
* Clear indication of the number of users who will be included in the segment before creation.

### 9.X Scope (v2.X) (WIP)

#### Background

While v2.3 introduced real-time capabilities with the SDK, many clients heavily rely on their existing GA4 setup for comprehensive web analytics. To deepen our integration and unlock more sophisticated marketing scenarios without requiring immediate SDK adoption, this version focuses on expanding our Journey triggers to support a wider range of standard and custom GA4 events.

By leveraging detailed GA4 events like scroll depth, form\_submit, and specific click actions, we empower marketers to create highly contextual and behavior-driven journeys. This allows them to react to nuanced user interest signals‚Äîsuch as deep engagement with a page or interaction with specific UI elements‚Äîand to seamlessly connect website form submissions with conversational follow-ups in LINE. This enhancement bridges the gap between web analytics and marketing automation, enabling more precise targeting and timely, personalized communication based on a richer understanding of user behavior.

#### Success Metric

* **Adoption:** ‚â• 15% of newly created journeys utilize at least one of the new GA4 custom event triggers or splits within the first 3 months of release.
* **Engagement:** A 10% increase in the usage of behavior-based journey splits (compared to only tag-based splits) among active journey users.

#### Feature list

* A - Trigger/Split Node: GA4 Custom Event Trigger

**A - Trigger/Split Node: GA4 Custom Event Trigger**

**User Story** As a marketer, I want to trigger journeys or create splits based on a wider range of specific GA4 events, so I can design more granular and responsive campaigns that react to nuanced customer behaviors and interests demonstrated on my website.

**Flow**

1. The user opens the Journey Builder interface.
2. When configuring a Trigger or a Split node, the user selects "GA4 Event" as the type.
3. A new dropdown menu appears, allowing the user to select from an expanded list of standard GA4 events.
4. Depending on the selected event, additional input fields appear to specify event parameters (e.g., page\_location for page\_view, or a CSS selector for click).
5. The user configures the parameters and saves the node.
6. The journey will now trigger or split based on the specified GA4 event and its associated parameters, allowing for highly contextual automation.

**Spec**

The following GA4 events will be supported as journey triggers and split conditions.

**1. Event: click**

* **Description:** Triggers when a user clicks on a link or element.
* **Use Case:** When a user clicks on a specific category (e.g., "Recommendations for 18‚Äì25"), a tag can be added in MAAC, enrolling them in a product journey designed for that age group.
* **Configurable Parameters:**
  * link\_classes: The CSS class of the clicked element.
  * link\_domain: The domain of the clicked link.
  * link\_url: The full URL of the clicked link.
  * outbound: Boolean (true if the link leads away from the current domain).

**2. Event: form\_submit**

* **Description:** Triggers upon successful submission of a form.
* **Use Case:** After a user completes a consultation or catalog request form, they can be immediately transferred to a live agent on LINE for a personal follow-up, bypassing the standard nurturing sequence.
* **Configurable Parameters:**
  * form\_id: The ID of the submitted form.
  * form\_name: The name of the submitted form.

**3. Event: page\_view**

* **Description:** Triggers when a user views a page. (Enhanced with location and referrer data).
* **Use Case:** Track which traffic sources and landing pages lead to key actions, allowing for user segmentation based on campaign, product, or referral source.
* **Configurable Parameters:**
  * page\_location: The full URL of the page being viewed. (Supports "contains" or "equals" matching).
  * page\_referrer: The URL of the referring page.

**4. Event: scroll**

* **Description:** Triggers when a user scrolls to a certain depth on a page.
* **Use Case:** If a user scrolls to 90% of a detailed page (like a course description), a LINE message can be triggered via MAAC to provide advanced information or a special offer, capitalizing on their demonstrated interest for real-time interaction.
* **Configurable Parameters:**
  * percent\_scrolled: Numeric value (e.g., 90).

**5. Events: session\_start / user\_engagement**

* **Description:** Triggers based on session initiation or engagement duration.
* **Use Case:**
  * session\_start: Identify returning visitors as a strong indicator of sustained interest.
  * user\_engagement: Evaluate the depth of interaction within a single visit (based on GA4's engagement time parameter). These metrics can define highly active users and trigger more frequent or personalized journeys in MAAC.
* **Configurable Parameters:**
  * session\_start: No parameters needed.
  * user\_engagement: engagement\_time\_msec (e.g., trigger if greater than 60000ms).

**6. Event: add\_to\_wishlist (Custom Event for "add to favorite product")**

* **Description:** Triggers when a user adds an item to their favorites or wishlist. This relies on the client implementing a custom add\_to\_wishlist event in their GA4 setup.
* **Use Case:** When a user favorites a product, a journey can be triggered to send a notification if that item goes on sale or comes back in stock, or to send a reminder after a few days.
* **Configurable Parameters:**
  * item\_id: The ID of the product added.
  * item\_name: The name of the product added.
  * value: The price of the item.

#### 2025.05.20 v2.1 clarifications for node performance

* Some questions raised by [Gideon Pan](mailto:gideon.pan@cresclab.com)
  * Block attribution: [https://chatbotgang.slack.com/archives/C08JZHN576Z/p1747380633203759?thread\_ts=1747205124.890269\&cid=C08JZHN576Z](https://chatbotgang.slack.com/archives/C08JZHN576Z/p1747380633203759?thread_ts=1747205124.890269\&cid=C08JZHN576Z)
  * Time filter: [https://chatbotgang.slack.com/archives/C08JZHN576Z/p1747383088430809?thread\_ts=1747205124.890269\&cid=C08JZHN576Z](https://chatbotgang.slack.com/archives/C08JZHN576Z/p1747383088430809?thread_ts=1747205124.890269\&cid=C08JZHN576Z)
  * Peter‚Äôs thoughts
    * Regarding **block attribution**topic
    * **IMO, the block info should be attributed to the closest node where users blocked the LINE OA.**
      * But let‚Äôs take a step back, why do marketers want to know the blocked info?
      * Because it helps them know if the marketing message is too annoying or not.
      * Hence, we should show the block info at two places
        * Overview: how many blocks caused by this entire journey
        * Node: blocked info should be attributed on the closest node where users block the LINE OA

For example, users pass node A -> node B -> node C ‚Üí blocked the LINE OA.

We should attribute the block info to ‚Äúnode C‚Äù.

*
  *
    * Regarding **time filter** topic
    * IMO, let‚Äôs not add the time filter at the moment.
      * Let‚Äôs also take a step back, why do marketers want to have a time filter?
      * Because it helps them analyze the trend.
      * I think the purpose of ‚Äúnode performance‚Äù is to let marketers understand the performance of this particular node.
      * Adding the time filter will make the behavior too complicated.
      * IMO, the best place to add a time filter is at a reporting dashboard or to leverage AI (in the future), that‚Äôs the right place for advanced analysis.
      * Hence, my decision is
        * If it is not difficult to add the time filter in the future (two-way door)
        * Then I will suggest not adding a time filter this time (v2.1).

| **ID**  | **Description**                                                                                                   | **Count** | **Total MRR** | **MRR per Requirement** |
| ------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | --------- | ------------- | ----------------------- |
| RC00486 | We hope to see the performance of each node in Journey 2.0.                                                       | 6         | 169963.0      | 28327.2                 |
| RC00173 | it's able to trigger customer journey by behavior.                                                                | 17        | 289644.0      | 17037.9                 |
| RC00504 | Want to know the number of people in each node and the list of users who can export to that node.                 | 3         | 46935.2       | 15645.1                 |
| RC00457 | I hope there will be an automatic notification mechanism (e.g. via email) when the prize is about to be sent out. | 3         | 46600.0       | 15533.3                 |
| RC00302 | Hope Journey can track open count                                                                                 | 2         | 25327.6       | 12663.8                 |
| RC00324 | Hope to add birthday condition in customer journey, and set the follow-up journey according to the birthday       | 3         | 37468.4       | 12489.5                 |
| RC00390 | Hope the customer journey can be set to trigger when there are multiple tags at the same time                     | 7         | 62400.0       | 8914.3                  |
| RC00019 | GA detects purchases and uses this data to tag friends automatically.                                             | 2         | 15373.4       | 7686.7                  |
| RC00153 | The customer journey "Tag added" can be set with multiple conditions at the same time                             | 2         | 12999.6       | 6499.8                  |
| RC00014 | Customer Journay can be integrated with DPM to send out                                                           | 4         | 24778.0       | 6194.5                  |

note: RC00486 and RC00504 can merge into 1 requirement.

* combined MRR per requirement: 24099.8

**v2.1 Internal Update**

Internal update: v2.1 Journey node performance

Node-level metrics to spot traffic bottlenecks, understand every step‚Äôs impact, and fine-tune journeys for deeper customer engagement.

| **PM Owner**            | [Peter Su](mailto:peter.su@cresclab.com) (deputy: [Jean Liu](mailto:jean.liu@cresclab.com) ) |
| ----------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| **Product**             | MAAC                                                                                         |
| **Region**              | All                                                                                          |
| **Target Release Date** | - Tier 1: 7/23 - Tier 2: 7/30 - Tier 3: 8/6                                                  |

### Background

* **Analytics is baseline**: Competitors (Omnichat, BotBonnie, Omnisegment) already have journey node metrics; this is table-stakes for marketers.
* \*\*Blind optimization:\*\*Marketers don‚Äôt know contact journey progress, so they guess when adjusting setups. Detailed node metrics provide missing visibility.
* \*\*AI Journey Foundation:\*\*This is the first milestone in our AI Journey and the foundation for our upcoming MAAC co-pilot.

### Introduction

Customer Journey node-level metrics provide an in-context dashboard on every step of a Journey.

* **What users see**
  * On every node (all types): Traffics (repeated events), Unique contacts
  * On message-sending nodes: + Messages pushed, Opens, Clicks, Unique clicks, Orders, Revenue
  * On Split nodes: % of traffic split to ‚ÄúYes/No‚Äù Split
  * Journey-level summary: Message pushed, Opens (%), Clicks (%), Unique clicks (%), GA events (add-to-cart, orders, revenue)
* **Where users see it**
  * Edit page ‚Äì provide users with immediate reference points to adjust nodes during the campaign.
  * Report page ‚Äì summary panel for an at-a-glance overview, with options to drill down and navigate the date range.

| Before                                                                                                                    | **Now** üÜï                                                                                                                |
| ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Edit page![](<../../../.gitbook/assets/Unknown image (74)>) Report page![](<../../../.gitbook/assets/Unknown image (75)>) | Edit page![](<../../../.gitbook/assets/Unknown image (76)>) Report page![](<../../../.gitbook/assets/Unknown image (77)>) |

#### Target Audience & Selling Points

* **Marketers** ‚Äì focus on customer engagement & conversions
  * Pain point

Need to keep journeys engaging and conversion-focused, but without step-by-step data they can‚Äôt tell which message, delay, or Split is dragging performance down.

*
  * **Selling point**

_Node metrics (traffic, opens, clicks, orders) spotlight drop-offs and high-performers in real time, so you can tweak copy, timing, or targeting during campaigns to optimize engagement and conversions._

* **CRM Managers** ‚Äì focus on customer LTV
  * Pain point

Without step-by-step data, they can‚Äôt pinpoint where members drop out, stall, or re-engage. This makes it hard to design precise retention, upgrade, or win-back nudges, and even harder to prove their impact.

*
  * **Selling point**_Node metrics pinpoint where members engage or drop out, enabling precise fixes that lift active member count and retention._

#### Scenario

* ### **Scenario #1: Delay reminder shows high opens but low clicks/orders**
  * User goal: Keep contacts engaged and ready to act
  * How:
    1. Marketer sees the ‚ÄúDelay 3 days ‚Üí Reminder‚Äù node with high opens but low clicks/orders.
    2. They shorten the delay to 1 day, republish, and test clicks improvement in the next few days.
* ### **Scenario #2: Funnel drops between ‚ÄúWebsite visit‚Äù and ‚ÄúAdd to Cart‚Äù**
  * User goal: Rescue traffic and increase checkout start
  * How:
    1. Node metrics show a sharp traffic fall after ‚Äúwebsite visit‚Äù to ‚ÄúAdd to Cart‚Äù node.
    2. Marketer broadens the preceding condition from ‚ÄúAdd to Cart‚Äù to ‚ÄúViewed specific product page‚Äù so more visitors enter the ‚Äúyes‚Äù spit Split.
    3. Verify higher traffic and conversions through the path.

#### Combine Feature

* **GA Integration** ‚Äì import website behaviors (page views, add-to-cart, checkout, etc.) into Journey metrics, linking on-site actions with each node‚Äôs performance.
* **SDK Event Tracking (coming soon)** ‚Äì stream real-time site events straight into Journey for instant triggers and up-to-the-second optimisation.

### Note & FAQ

#### Note

* **Data update frequency**
  * Metrics refresh hourly.
* **Journey editing limits**
  * Once a journey is published, the node structure is locked: you cannot add or delete nodes.
  * You may pause the journey and adjust node conditions (e.g., delay days, audience filters).
  * Trigger settings are locked. Changing them prompts the system to duplicate the journey, so you can re-configure and publish a new version.
* **How metrics behave after edits**
  * The platform does not keep version history; metrics continue accumulating on the edited nodes.
  * If you need separate metrics for each configuration, clone the journey first or keep your own timestamped notes for comparison.
* **Only journey created after v2.1 (2025.08.11) will have node metrics**
  * **Context:** ENG changed the data source from MAAC-only data to CL-wide Engagement History data to enable CL-wide data applications and simplify data management through centralization.
  * Due to this change in the data source, the following limitations apply to node metrics.

![](<../../../.gitbook/assets/Unknown image (83)>)

| Journey created time | For the journey created **BEFORE** node performance release date (2025/8/11)                          | For the journey created **AFTER** node performance release date (2025/8/11)                                        |
| -------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| Data source          | Use the current journey data source                                                                   | Use the new journey data source                                                                                    |
| Node metrics         | Without node metrics                                                                                  | With node metrics                                                                                                  |
| How users feel?      | Users won't feel any difference after this release.![](<../../../.gitbook/assets/Unknown image (80)>) | Users will find the node performance metrics after this release.![](<../../../.gitbook/assets/Unknown image (81)>) |

#### FAQ

_**Q1. Do I need to enable anything?**_

* No. Node-level metrics appear automatically on all new **and** existing journeys.

_**Q2. How fresh is the data?**_

* Metrics refresh **hourly**.

_**Q3. Will historical data be back-filled?**_

* **Yes, for most metrics.** The system will back-process historical journey traffic, sent, opens, clicks, orders, and revenue.
* **Exception:** **Unique Clicks** and **Unique CTR** start accumulating only from **2025-07-07** and are **not** back-filled.

_**Q4. Which metrics appear on each node?**_

* **Yes.** The system back-processes _all_ node metrics‚Äîtraffic, sent, opens, clicks, **unique clicks/CTR**, orders, and revenue‚Äîso past journeys show complete data from day one of the feature.

_**Q5. What if I need a new node or a different trigger?**_

* Duplicate the journey, make the structural changes, and publish the new version.

### Setting (For CSM)

No need for CSM setting

Q from Dash

1. Â†±Ë°®È†ÅÂèØ‰ª•ÂåØÂá∫ÂóéÔΩû‰∏çË°å
2. ÈáùÂ∞çÊóÖÁ®ãÂ¶ÇÊûú‰øÆÊîπ‰∏çÊúÉÊúâ logÔºåUI ÊúÉ‰∏çÊúÉÊèêÈÜíÁî®Êà∂ > ÊúÉ
3. ÁõÆÂâç node ÊàêÊïàÊúÉÊúâÊ¨äÈôê view ÁöÑÂ∑ÆÁï∞Âóé > ‰∏çÊúÉÂΩ±Èüø

**v2.2 User Story & Test Case**

### 9.2 Scope (v2.2)

#### User Stories

**Time-Based Triggers**

* **\[P0]** As a marketer, I can schedule a journey to start on a specific future date and time, so that I can prepare time-sensitive campaigns in advance.
* **\[P0]** As a marketer, I can configure a time-based trigger to target a specific user segment, so that my scheduled campaigns reach the correct audience.
* **\[P0]** As a marketer, I can set a single recurring frequency for a journey (i.e., daily, weekly, or monthly), so that I can automate regular communications like weekly updates or monthly newsletters.
* **\[P0]** As a system administrator, I can ensure the user segment for a recurring journey is evaluated a fixed time before each execution, so that the journey starts on time without being delayed by last-minute processing.
* **\[P1]** As a marketer, when setting a weekly recurrence, I can select one or more specific days of the week, so that I have precise control over my campaign schedule.
* **\[P1]** As a marketer, when setting a monthly recurrence, I can select one or more specific days of the month, so that I can align with events like paydays or subscription renewals.
* **\[P1]** As a marketer, I can set an optional end date for a recurring trigger, so that campaigns automatically stop after a promotion period has concluded.

**Add/Remove Tag Node**

* **\[P0]** As a marketer, I can add a node to my journey that **adds** one or more tags to a user who reaches it, so that I can categorize users based on their journey behavior.
* **\[P1]** As a marketer, I can add a node to my journey that **removes** one or more tags from a user who reaches it, so that I can maintain an accurate and effective set of tags on my contacts.
* **\[P0]** As a system, when an attempt is made to add a tag a user already has (or remove one they don't), I will log the event and allow the user to proceed without error, so that journeys are robust and operators have visibility into all attempts.
* **\[P2 - Not in v2.2]** As a marketer, I can select tags to add or remove from MAAC, CAAC, or CDH tag sources in a single interface, so that I can manage user data consistently across platforms.

**Journey Performance Metrics**

* **\[P0]** As a marketer, I can view the total number of times a time-based trigger has fired and the number of unique contacts who entered through it, so that I can evaluate the effectiveness of my scheduled campaigns.
* **\[P0]** As a marketer, I can view performance metrics on the Add/Remove Tag node, so that I can confirm my user categorization is working as expected.
* **\[P0]** As a marketer, I can view the traffic count through each path of an engagement-based Split, so that I can analyze the performance of my message content and calls to action.

**Non-Functional Requirements**

* **\[P1]** As an engineer, I want the journey trigger and execution system to be performant and scalable, so that it can handle large user segments and high-frequency schedules without delays or failures. \[NFR-P0-1]
* **\[P1]** As a data engineer, I want journey performance metrics to be accurate and processed efficiently, so that marketers can trust the reports. \[NFR-P1-2]

* üìù **\[Infra/BE]** \[NFR-P0-1-Test3]: (Reliability) Simulate a server failure (e.g., kill a pod) during the segment evaluation process.
  * **Expected Result:** The system recovers and either completes the evaluation successfully or safely retries, ensuring no users are lost or processed twice.

  * **Expected Result:** No users are "lost" in the metric pipeline. SUM(node\_N\_outputs) == SUM(node\_N-1\_outputs).
* üìù **\[DE]** \[NFR-P1-2-Test2]: (Performance) Measure the data latency for metrics to appear in the UI after an action occurs.
  * **Expected Result:** Node counts are updated in the reporting UI within a specified time frame (e.g., 1 hour ) of the event.

**v2.2 Internal Update**

## Journey v2.2

Automate and personalize customer journeys with intelligent scheduling, real-time engagement Split, and dynamic audience tagging.

| **Latest update**       | The Segment Trigger in Journey has been a long-requested feature from GTM. However, during stress testing, triggering a segment with 1M audience members caused excessive system load. Considering both the test results and the overall Journey architecture, we have decided not to proceed with this feature's release at this stage.Following multiple discussions on enhancements related to Journey v2.2, the current direction is as follows: - \[Journey v2.2 - 1] Follow/unfollow LINE Event Trigger in Journey - Scheduled for Tiered Release starting 8/26. - \[Journey v2.2 - 2] Segment: Add & Remove Tag - As this cannot be fully automated to meet real-time business scenarios, it will be placed in the backlog. - Some related needs (e.g., quick campaign setups) still exist, so timeline is TBD. - \[Journey v2.2 - 3] Rich Menu Switch by Segment \[Outsourced] - Although the current focus is LINE, demand remains strong. - This feature will be handled by an outsourcing partner, with the release date TBD. |

### Background

In today's competitive digital landscape, personalization at scale is no longer a luxury‚Äîit's an expectation. Marketers are moving away from generic, one-off campaign "blasts" and toward creating continuous, automated conversations that adapt to a user's behavior over their entire lifecycle. The core market trend is a shift towards efficiency and intelligence: delivering the right message to the right person at the right time, without exhaustive manual effort.

Our company-level strategy focuses on deepening customer engagement and increasing Customer Lifetime Value (LTV). Journey v2.2 is a critical step in this direction. Previously, our Journey feature was a powerful tool for building campaign flows, but it often required manual activation and followed a static path.

We built Journey v2.2 to solve our clients' most pressing automation challenges. They told us they were spending too much time manually scheduling weekly newsletters, couldn't easily identify and reward their most engaged users in real-time, and lacked a simple way to clean up user segments based on journey interactions. Journey v2.2 directly addresses this by transforming our Journey feature from a simple campaign tool into an intelligent, "set it and forget it" marketing automation engine that drives the entire customer lifecycle. The primary business driver for this update was to unblock automated, segment-based Rich Menu switching‚Äîa highly requested and powerful feature for personalization.

### Introduction

**Journey v2.2: Time-based (target specific segment) Triggers & Engagement Split** **& Add/Remove Tag node**is a significant enhancement to our core marketing automation Journey feature. It introduces three new, powerful node types that work in concert to create truly dynamic, responsive, and timely customer experiences.

üÜö **Optimization for: Journey Automation & Workflow** This update is a major optimization of the marketer's workflow. It moves from a basic trigger system to a fully automated one.

| **Original Functionality**                         | **v2.2 Optimization**                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  |
| -------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Journey starts with simple event triggers.         | Time-Based Triggers: "Set-and-forget" scheduling with daily, weekly, or monthly recurrence.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            |
| User attributes were static within a journey flow. | Add/Remove Tag Node: Dynamically re-segment users based on their behavior within the journey to empower the personalization.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           |
| Only support LINE msg open event trigger           | Follow/unfollow LINE Event Trigger in Journey:**Engage New Friends Instantly:** "Trigger a welcome journey the moment a user adds your LINE OA. Deliver an introductory offer or guided onboarding to boost conversion from day one."**Win Back and Understand Churn:** "When a user blocks your LINE OA, automatically trigger a journey to reach them on another channel like email or SMS. Gather feedback with a survey or present a win-back offer to maintain the relationship." |

**Primary:** Digital Marketers, Marketing Automation Specialists.

**Personas:**

* **"Time-Poor Tanya":** Manages multiple campaigns and channels. Her biggest need is efficiency. She wants to automate recurring tasks (like weekly promotions) so she can focus on strategy. She values tools that are reliable and easy to set up.
* **"Data-Driven David":** Focused on metrics and ROI. His biggest need is to prove the effectiveness of his campaigns. He wants to segment his audience based on behavior to improve open/click rates and personalize offers for "hot leads" vs. "inactive users."

**Needs & Pains:**

* **Pain:** Manually exporting lists and scheduling recurring campaigns each week/month.**Need:** An automated, reliable scheduler.
* **Pain:** User segments become stale and outdated.**Need:** A method to dynamically update user profiles based on their real-world actions.
* **Pain:** A slow, disconnected response to new followers. **Need:** An instant way to engage new followers to improve onboarding and retention.
* **Pain:** Losing contact with users who block the LINE account. **Need:** An automated way to re-engage users on other channels and understand churn reasons.

**Selling Points:**

You'll save hours every week and ensure consistent, timely communication with your audience without ever lifting a finger."                                                                                                                                                                                                                 |

This keeps your audiences perfectly updated for hyper-personalized follow-ups and Rich Menu experiences."                                                                                                                                                                                       |

Deliver an introductory offer or guided onboarding to boost conversion from day one."**Win Back and Understand Churn:** "When a user blocks your LINE OA, automatically trigger a journey to reach them on another channel like email or SMS. (will be supported soon) Gather feedback with a survey or present a win-back offer to maintain the relationship." |
